
============== high level task decomposition ================
[{'objective': 'Analyze the properties of the convex equilateral hexagon with opposite sides parallel to establish relationships between its sides and angles'}, {'objective': "Express the directions and lengths of the hexagon's sides using vectors or coordinate geometry to model the hexagon"}, {'objective': 'Determine the geometric relationship between the triangle formed by the extensions of sides AB, CD, and EF and the hexagon'}, {'objective': "Use the given side lengths of the triangle (200, 240, 300) to set up equations relating to the hexagon's side length"}, {'objective': 'Solve the resulting system of equations to find the side length of the hexagon'}]
============== task analysis ================
1. Extract and Summarize Given Information:
- The figure is a convex equilateral hexagon ABCDEF, meaning all its sides have equal length.
- The hexagon has the property that all pairs of opposite sides are parallel. Since it is a hexagon, opposite sides are AB and DE, BC and EF, CD and FA.
- A triangle is formed by the extensions of segments AB, CD, and EF. The sides of this triangle have lengths 200, 240, and 300.
- The objective is to find the common side length of the hexagon.

2. Analyze Relationships Between Components:
- The hexagon is equilateral and has pairs of opposite sides parallel, implying it is a special type of hexagon, often called an affine-regular or equilateral hexagon with parallel opposite sides.
- The triangle formed by the extensions of AB, CD, and EF suggests these three lines (or their extensions) intersect pairwise to form a triangle outside or around the hexagon.
- The side lengths of this triangle (200, 240, 300) correspond to distances between intersection points of these extended lines.
- The parallelism and equal side length conditions impose strong geometric constraints, likely relating the hexagon’s side length to the triangle’s side lengths.

3. Identify the Field of Study:
- The problem lies primarily in Euclidean geometry, specifically polygon geometry and properties of convex polygons.
- It involves concepts of parallel lines, convex polygons, and properties of line intersections.
- The problem may also touch on affine geometry or vector geometry due to parallelism and side length constraints.
- Such problems are common in mathematical competitions and advanced geometry studies.

4. Highlight Aspects Needing Clarification:
- The exact configuration of the hexagon (e.g., orientation, coordinates) is not specified.
- The position of the triangle formed by the extensions of AB, CD, and EF relative to the hexagon is not explicitly described.
- It is not stated whether the triangle formed is inside or outside the hexagon, or how the extensions intersect.
- Assumptions about convexity and the order of vertices are given, but the problem may require assuming a standard labeling or orientation.
- The problem assumes the hexagon is equilateral and convex with parallel opposite sides, which restricts its shape but does not fully determine it without further assumptions.

Each side has length s, so the side vectors are s*u, s*v, s*w (with appropriate signs depending on orientation). We choose a coordinate system by placing vertex A at the origin (0,0). The pairs of opposite sides are (AB || DE), (BC || EF), and (CD || FA). This implies the hexagon has three distinct directions for its sides, each direction corresponding to a pair of parallel sides. We assign vectors u, v, w to represent the directions of sides AB, BC, and CD respectively. Since opposite sides are parallel, DE is parallel to AB, so DE is in direction u; EF is parallel to BC, so EF is in direction v; and FA is parallel to CD, so FA is in direction w. Each side has length s, so the side vectors are s*u, s*v, s*w (with appropriate signs depending on orientation). We choose a coordinate system by placing vertex A at the origin (0,0).
